    <a title="Eva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84556572-eva"><img alt="Eva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547210975p2/84556572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2693926333?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva" href="/user/show/84556572-eva">Eva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84556572-eva?shelf=manga-comics">manga-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2693926333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9244799210868835203">I must say that my first interaction with the universe of GitS was the 1995 film. So when I first started reading this I was put off by how much of a different character the major was. The whole book is much more light-hearted than the film.<br/><br/>For the most part it is more of an episodic work. We start in-media-res and the feeling of that only really goes away at the end as we go through snippets of life in section 9 and in this sci-fi future. You don't really get to understand all the context, and </span>
  <span id="freeText9244799210868835203" style="display:none">I must say that my first interaction with the universe of GitS was the 1995 film. So when I first started reading this I was put off by how much of a different character the major was. The whole book is much more light-hearted than the film.<br /><br />For the most part it is more of an episodic work. We start in-media-res and the feeling of that only really goes away at the end as we go through snippets of life in section 9 and in this sci-fi future. You don't really get to understand all the context, and there's some small (author or translator's?) notes explaining things throughout the whole work which help a lot, but ultimately you don't really need to know everything about the universe. Eventually I reached a middle point where the brand/model number gibberish is scarce enough that stopped feeling bad for filtering it out.<br />As I said this is more of an episodic work, with only the latter chapters making up a longer narrative. Due to this you could say the writing matures throughout the book, as you go from small chapters with things like that lesbian scene on the boat (with the most contrasting dialogue ever) to longer chapters about finding out who the bad guys are amidst all the politics.<br /><br />The art-style isn't one of my favourites but it was fitting and worked out for both machinery and people. <br />As far as panelling goes, I had a lot of trouble figuring out what happened in close-quarters action scenes. Who came from where and what are they doing? Sometimes it felt like we were missing a panel in the middle, or would benefit from seeing the thoughts of a character. <br />The colour choices, giving some pages a colourful oily look, and mostly dabbing on dark tones with strong contrast of cold and warm colours were really good though. Really gives the vibe of big artificial polluted city.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9244799210868835203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9672825164099807362">Something different, but I was curious to (finally) read it before the new (live) action movie comes out relatively soon. (Although, as I understand it, the new movie is a re-make of the original anime (animated) movie, which doesn't fully track the book anyway.)<br/><br/>I admit I don't read much manga, so - for me - it's "just another" graphic novel from around the same period (late 1980's into the early 1990's) in which graphic novels and adult comic books began to hit their stride in the U.S., followi</span>
  <span id="freeText9672825164099807362" style="display:none">Something different, but I was curious to (finally) read it before the new (live) action movie comes out relatively soon. (Although, as I understand it, the new movie is a re-make of the original anime (animated) movie, which doesn't fully track the book anyway.)<br /><br />I admit I don't read much manga, so - for me - it's "just another" graphic novel from around the same period (late 1980's into the early 1990's) in which graphic novels and adult comic books began to hit their stride in the U.S., following on, and riding the tide of creativity and success including everything from <i>Maus</i>, <i>The Dark Knight Returns</i>, <i>Sandman</i>, and the iconic <i>Watchmen</i>, to Alex Ross's gorgeous work in <i>Marvels</i>, <i>Kingdom Come</i>, and even the large format <i>Peace on Earth</i>.<br /><br />It's far more sci-fi (with a nod to cyberpunk, and heavy on the artificial intelligence angle) and conspiracy theory than super-hero fare, and the geo-politics are kind of fun since they're seen through a 25-year-old Japanese filter. As for the story, well, frankly, I found it a bit hard to follow or get terribly emotionally vested in.<br /><br />I wish I'd read it when it was new, and I was less jaded by nearly three decades of increasingly good graphic novel literature (and I don't use the word "literature" lightly), particularly including some of the newer sublime work such as the highly acclaimed <i>Persepolis</i>, <i>Terminal Lance: The White Donkey</i>, and even <i>Strong Female Protagonist</i>.<br /><br />As for whether I'll bother to see the movie, well, time will tell.</span>

    <a title="Olgalijo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4873843-olgalijo"><img alt="Olgalijo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384659979p2/4873843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer899308201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4608665445255337077">This is one of those cult authors who have people telling you all over how good they are. I disagree. Completely. Yes, he applies some pretty hard core ethical dilemmas to the future world, but that's it. The artwork is just ugly, and not especially original, apart from the changes from black and white to color (and to tell you the truth, it looks more like he wanted color but was too lazy to follow up on it). The plot is difficult to follow, not because the ideas are so complicated, but because</span>
  <span id="freeText4608665445255337077" style="display:none">This is one of those cult authors who have people telling you all over how good they are. I disagree. Completely. Yes, he applies some pretty hard core ethical dilemmas to the future world, but that's it. The artwork is just ugly, and not especially original, apart from the changes from black and white to color (and to tell you the truth, it looks more like he wanted color but was too lazy to follow up on it). The plot is difficult to follow, not because the ideas are so complicated, but because the panels are poorly chosen and ordered. Moreover, the insistence on drawing almost completely naked female bodies in every page and scores of violent scenes reminds me of the teenage boy equivalent of the likes of Diana Gabaldon and Jane Auer. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2019519000205044562"><br/>3/5 Stars<br/><br/>I wanted to love this manga. I really, really did. I'm a big fan of manga and anime from the 80s and 90s (<i>Akira</i> is a personal favorite), and I love the feature-length anime film based on the <i> Ghost in the Shell</i> series.   <span id="freeText2019519000205044562" style="display:none"><br />3/5 Stars<br /><br />I wanted to love this manga. I really, really did. I'm a big fan of manga and anime from the 80s and 90s (<i>Akira</i> is a personal favorite), and I love the feature-length anime film based on the <i> Ghost in the Shell</i> series. But the manga really failed to capture me in quite the same way.<br />The art was fantastic and Major Kusanagi was as snappy as ever, but I found the story incredibly difficult to follow and it seemed to lack the hint of darkness that gives the anime its dimension. I'm hoping that the second volume will be an improvement, but I was left a bit disappointed by this installment.<br /><br />All in all, not bad, and worth reading for it's classic status and wonderful 80s art- but I think most people would be just fine watching the movie.</span>

<div id="review_2925702355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2925702355" />

        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/56446521-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781632364210" href="/book/show/31415835-the-ghost-in-the-shell-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2925702355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10278593073732807426">This manga is like the anime but also very different. The anime does feature some scenes from the manga and overall they do cover some of the same topics - but the tones are very different. This book is a little on the lighter side, especially some of the author notes are pretty funny. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a2UK2ptyEaukXDZo9NGn39PzgtYAXwSgnfCqW9Cohu1pzaD0IjYMWVRzss69LNud65hfTm8GfEY0dGd1U+NpbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('njFVk6JfjVqIJ7zIrfHkaD9aK4znKs0QcYzNuha8MrCcmf+9GxuQqHgIOG7kDJgqBzH2FIhztfbYCACUlffdMA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13036412352935517765">Masamune Shirow (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14791271._____' title='士郎 正宗' rel='nofollow noopener'>士郎 正宗</a>) is an internationally renowned manga artist. He is best known for the manga Ghost in the Shell, which has since been turned into two theatrical anime movies, two anime TV series, an anime TV movie, and several video games. Shirow is also known for creating erotic art.<br/>Born in the Hyōgo Prefecture capital city of Kobe, he studied oil painting at Osaka University of Arts. Whil</span>
  <span id="freeText13036412352935517765" style="display:none">Masamune Shirow (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14791271._____" title="士郎 正宗" rel="nofollow noopener">士郎 正宗</a>) is an internationally renowned manga artist. He is best known for the manga Ghost in the Shell, which has since been turned into two theatrical anime movies, two anime TV series, an anime TV movie, and several video games. Shirow is also known for creating erotic art.<br />Born in the Hyōgo Prefecture capital city of Kobe, he studied oil painting at Osaka University of Arts. While in college, he developed an interest in manga, which led him to create his own complete work, Black Magic, which was published in the manga fanzine Atlas. His work caught the eye of Seishinsha President Harumichi Aoki, who offered to publish him. The result was Appleseed, a full volume of densely-plotted drama taking place in an ambiguous future. The story was a sensation, and won the 1986 Seiun Award for Best Manga. After a professional reprint of Black Magic and a second volume of Appleseed, he released Dominion in 1986. Two more volumes of Appleseed followed before he began work on Ghost in the Shell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13036412352935517765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
